You remember that feeling as a kid when having watched a ghibli movie for the first time, Not knowing there are more of that sort, that those cartoons origin from Japan, where they are called anime.   As someone who watched anime for several years now I come to appriciate shows that don't go with the typical anime. Shows that aren't predictable. moments that feel orginal. Moments that aren't solely here to prove that this is "anime". Moments that make you feel like you're actually watching a story because of the story aspect, without the need of throwing in typical anime tropes.   This is a show I know I can recommend people that don't like Anime, bacause I know that this show just tells a story, which people will appriciate, wether it actually is an anime or not dosen't even Matter bacause of how good it is.

i agree with most of the assessment, with the exception of Gundam.Even though it felt like a major release, the show feel more like Gundam Reconguista in G. The gundam design, the eyes are larger, the proportion, the armory, the color scheme, all of it. If you want to talk about corporation, Gundam IBO also does that, so this idea is not unique. For AAA gundam series, normally the storyline and MC has a sense of danger in it, either dangerous surrounding like war, or battle of survival, or the character is dangerous, like Wing and IBO. But here i dont feel it here, the setting is in a classroom, like a typical japanese anime story, the battle is in mock battlefield. Even though there is a risk, but it is not like real death, the only thing u lose is your face and reputation, so there are no real stake in it.  So all i can say is Gundam Mercury is a disappointment when compare to other AAA gundam series. It on its own is fine, but when u attach the name gundam, and u set your story in classroom, that just blew it away.  AAA Gundam example : gundam IBO, seed series, wing, 00, unicorn series (or UC series). Even Mobile Fighter G Gundam is better than this.

The world cup was legit the most fun Iâ€™ve had watching anything on TV in like the past 3 years. Glad you brought it up, because it really was more anime than anime itself. We got Japan as the hardcore underdog that turns it around at the last second against amazing teams like something out of old school inazuma 11. At the very bottom, at the point where there is no deeper level nor a single further foot that can be descended, Riko will find the end of her journey. There will not be a happy ending. Only the memories she brought with her along the way. The friendships developed, bonds forged, and companions who stand around her, knowing that this is the end Riko would have chosen given a thousand chances and the knowledge of the end that awaited her. Trapped, at the bottom of the Abyss, and only death awaits. We will be left to think about all those moments of hope, and love, and the indomitable spirit of one little girl who made the descent knowing it would inevitably lead to her death. His point about Bocchi the Rock needs to be hammered onto studios, creators and especially, audiences. Animation should shine as animation. They can do things that movies can't. Animations can learn from movies, but it must make use of the unique characteristics it has that movies can't replicate yet even with CGI. Art shifts, style, layering, interesting cut, strange transition, colour and so on are things that movies just can't do yet.   Video games are also suffering from the same problem. Somehow, animation and video games are "childish" and needs to be more "cinematics" to be taken seriously. That's ridiculous to me and is the equivalent of treating movies as childish because literature is the real grown up form of art. The work should explore and exploit its medium while learning from others. Directors like Shinkai who don't make use of animation as a medium is doing a disservice to everyone.

Okay that dropping the soundtrack during the Gundam segment, made me want to watch it.  I also had no ideia Made In Abyss S2 had come out
There's something sublime about Made in Abyss, which I haven't really experienced in any other anime... or really anything, at least not since I've been an adult. And season two took it to a level only hinted at in season one. Part of it is certainly that it juxtaposes Ghibli-esque beauty, moe-blob characters and moments that are dark or gory. Yes, it has all of that, but the sum is far greater.   It has adventure too, but it also feels more cohesive than many adventures with big worlds, less ad hoc. If One Piece or Hunter x Hunter are Minecraft or No Man's Sky with a world that expands because the show continues - procedurally generated... Made in Abyss feels more like Breath of the Wild - it's a vast world, but it feels purposeful, deliberate. And even then, the world is strange and unsettling - unsettling to your sense of reality and the possible, even as it makes an eerie sense. And like an archaeological dig, each new layer (of the story and the Abyss) re-contextualises what has gone before.   And of course, we can't not mention the Kevin of it all. His work on Made in Abyss is truly an example of the soundtrack elevating the work - and this work didn't need much elevating. The music is just so awesomely evocative. The only other comparable work I can think of in otherworldly power is perhaps Yuki Kajiura's work on Madoka Magica, though I think Mr Penkin has surpassed even that. 'The First Layer' has become as iconic for me as something like the Star Wars fanfare by John Williams.   There were so many great shows this year, but I can't fault Garnt for his number one. Even as I was swept away episode after episode by Kaguya, caught off-guard by Bocchi, or riding the hype train for Chainsaw Man... it never really felt like there was a true challenger to Made in Abyss.

Made in Abyss trully managed to encapsulate the feel of the Abyss, even to the viewer that is confortably seeing it from safety. The whole story until now has been repeating this idea that the abyss is not just a place of nightmares, but also dreams. It may be a horrifying place, but only in its darkness can you reveal the brightness it holds. This is the reason why our main characters never give up despite everything, and the reason we still watch hoping for them to succeed, despite knowing full well that their journey is doomed from the start.
Aight. I'm just here to say y'all have been sleeping on Iruma-kun for too long. Objectively speaking, I would rank it as close to Avatar the Last Airbender as anything else I've ever seen. It's a feel good anime but it still has strong ass character growth, wicked animation, and a complex cast of three-dimensional characters that includes both gay and non-binary representation in the most genuine way I've seen in anime that isn't specifically categorized under yuri or yaoi. For all good series, originals and not, I do strongly believe that Lycoris Recoil deserves more recognition by the wider audience (and I am not saying this due to position 15).   It's a truly perfect series for an anime original 12 episode run. It builds its main cast, delivers several selfcontained episodes that evenetually allow the main plot to arise and the characters to grow.  It also didn't shy away from some good ol' anime violence to actually happen on screen, which actually allows you to consider the possibility that someone from the main cast would really die.   It just... Works flawlessly as a selfcontained anime original, showing that it can be done and it can be high quality visually speaking.   Also, while at a surface level Majima is a wannabe Joker idiot, he has way more depth to his character.  I mean, he is a terrorist and all, but the Lycoris are effectively illegal black-ops child soldiers raised by the governement to fucking murder people, are used as expandable and their existence would be denied to the public.  The Japan of this world is pretty creepy if you think about it.  Addionally, he is also another type of strange character: a man with a strong presence and intense interactions with a girl in a Yuri dynamic. You really don't get to see many of those, even more if he is a true challenge for her and surpasses by far the other girl of the couple when It comes to combat.   I wouldn't go as far as calling it my favourite anime of the year... But yeah, It would rank high. Quite high. More I think about it, more my appreciation for it grows.  Also extreme big fucking disagree about MiA S2, but that's another topic.  I prefer the film by a long shot for several reasons. This season sets up such an interesting setting for the first 5/6 episodes and then, rather than exploring it, it's used for the personal character arc of a new entry to the group. One that the author tried so hard to make me believe she was right but doesn't have the balls to stick with the final conflict, giving the easy way out of "The villagers are actually fine with being murdered".

I'm surprised Komi didn't get a shoutout. I know some people had issues with the animation in Part 2, but I thought it was great start to finish.  Ranking of Kings was also excellent. It's quite a bold move to choose a mute protagonist, but Boji is the real deal, and the relationships we see throughout the series are just incredible. Every character has an arc and growth, and you so rarely can guess where a character will end up. Daida seems like he's just going to be a Joffrey character, but his arc is far deeper than that. And while Hilling initially comes off as the typical evil stepmother, she ends up being one of the characters you root for the most.  My anime of the year is probably Spy x Family though. I was an avid reader of the manga and the anime didn't disappoint. If anything, it exceeded my expectations and expanded upon some previously sparse scenes from the manga. Plus, it's such a funny, heartwarming tale that's beautifully written, animated, and scored. Seriously, all the OPs and EDs are such bangers.

I think part of what makes Chainsaw Man such a hit is that is effectively doing to Shounen what Evangelion did to Mecha.  Eccentric creator pours massive amounts of talent into a series with a main character who is the polar opposite of the norm for the status quo within its genre, especially one that is and would be irritating in real life. It doesn't hold back the darker, or even sexual themes while not glorifying them as most shows do. It's unconventional in it's approach to storytelling, characters, themes, and is not afraid to embrace it.  Both have Waifus that have hit the community like a fucking freight train.  Both are easily marketable.   Both have a simple initial premise that has FAR more going on than the story would openly admit.  So, they're completely genre-flipping titles that are easy to get into, have the bait to spread like wildfire within the community, incredibly popular music, but also have complex themes beneath the surface for those who wish to read into things, both made by eccentric creators who's stories' aren't afraid to take the simple concept to the logical extreme for the sake of the story... even at the expense of the audience itself.  I genuinely think we might be seeing Eva's successor, depending on where the story goes and ends... it could be *THAT* special.  I've followed along with it with my GF, and we've been enjoying it a lot to say the least. It's a good way to break her into that style of story. I'm hoping to get her into Eva eventually.

made in abyss may actually be my favorite anime. it's.. hard to really describe why. there's a passion to the story. each character is defined as their own character. you never see yourself making the same decisions they would make. motivating each other the way they do. you simple watch and wait to see what happens next while a part of you prays nothing bad happens the to charges l characters you love. Because that's what this show makes you feel. you're not rooting for these characters to succeed. you want them to go home. to be in a protected space where you can breathe easily. but you know that can't happen. so you cheer for their little wins while begging and pleading for them to be safe.   Maybe that's why this show is so hard to describe. because how do you describe what it feels like to be a parent as you watch your kids step into the world on their own?

Spy 10 family
Everyone knows that the real way to say Spy X Family is: the cross product of spy and family  Edit: After thinking about it for a bit, this unironically actually makes a lot of sense. So hear me out: the anime is essentially showcasing the PRODUCT of CROSSing the two very different concepts of spy and family as Loid forms a fake family. In addition, it makes sense mathematically as the magnitude of the resulting vector is the two vectors multiplied which reflects Loid's exponential increase in workload, causing him to be tired as shown in the anime. The direction of the resulting vector is also perpendicular to the original two vectors which indicates the change in direction of Loid, Yor, and Anya's life due to the formation of a fake family.

As a person who loves Made in abyss i love to see it being gigguks favorite anime of the year.
Made in Abyss has been an amazing journey. The manga is incredible with its beautiful, gritty frames. The anime is spectacular and moving with some of the best soundtracks I've ever heard. I'm constantly astounded that the voice acting keeps up and does it justice. It absolutely deserves its place and yet I'm blown away to see it so highly rated. I'm one of those people who never watches shows or movies more than once, no matter how much I like them. Even over a decade later I failed to fully watch back through Cowboy Bebop, one of my all time favorites. Yet I've watched Made in Abyss season 1 three separate times with different friends and season 2 I re-watched the first half so I could finish it with friends. Not a single episode the whole way had me pulling out my phone or feeling bored. I've put the OST from season 1 on in the background enough times it's almost in Final Fantasy territory. I still flip every time I'm watching a video and I hear someone put Made in Abyss in the background of even completely unrelated content. I just cannot sing the praises of the show enough. Here's hoping the slow manga progress and premature Season 3 announcement don't herald a drop in quality.

My list is mostly the same except for the ones I haven't seen or completed yet. Bocchi the Rock and Call of the Night are at the top for me, because I appreciate nothing more than creatively elevating a stale genre to new levels, or cultivating an immaculate vibe. The thing about Call of the Night is that it spends all this time cultivating this vibe, only to deliberately taint it near the end of the season, and remind you that while the night can be beautiful, dangers lurk in the darkness, and if you want to be the kind of person who can handle those dangers, you have to become something else. It promises that, if there's a season two, whatever comes will be very different, but just as brilliant.   The only things not mentioned here that I'm really high on are Teasing Master Takagi-san s3, The Demon Girl Next Door s2, Romantic Killer, and Do It Yourself, but most of those aren't Gigguk's thing, and I fully recognize those all individually hit for me in a way they may not for everyone. Well, I think Romantic Killer could have had a broader audience if it wasn't on Netflix. I related to it as someone not particularly interested in dating, and it surprised me with strong animation, funny jokes, and an extremely charismatic protagonist voiced to perfection. It did turn a bit dark near the end in a way that I didn't 100% like, though, but it averted any toxic messaging in favor of a really positive, rare message.   Demon Girl Next Door is really slept on, probably because it just looks like a cutesy slice of life with supernatural elements. But it gets surprisingly subversive the deeper it goes, and proves you don't have to be edgy at all to pick apart a genre. The lore is dark as hell if you stop for a moment to think about it, and the show KNOWS that but never rubs it in your face or tries to milk it. It's a fluffy show that acknowledges the existence of darkness and refuses to give the darkness any real foothoold. The sentimental and sweet moments feel more earned because we know the main characters have suffered genuine pain and hardship. and as it goes on it develops a great cast of funny supporting characters. and, I should mention too, it has an ongoing plot that advances slowly but steadily, with major, emotionally affecting revelations, and one genuinely gobsmacking twist that also doubles as one of the funniest jokes in the series. but it's not for everyone and I totally get that only some people are going to be able to get on its wavelength.

W list, L clorox fans for being salty that their favorite ain't on Gigguks listğŸ˜‚typical Bitchigo behavior
If I can at least try to convey the feeling of Made in Abyss that it at least gave to me...  I have seen a lot of anime. Over 400 anime, and while to some that may not be much by comparison, it's enough for many. I have seen the good, the bad, and the terribly ugly.   I have seen Boku no Pico all the way through, because I felt I needed to see every spectrum of anime, even trash shows like Mars of Destruction, to have a an accurate view of what anime is and every type of anime out there. I sat through it unblinking, hating every second of it, but in the grand scope of things, it was still relatively easy to bear through. I've seen gore, to monsters, from Monster to Galactic Heroes.  When I watched Season 1 of Made in Abyss, it was everything and more than I was (or could be) expecting, and when I finished, I felt like a broken man, one that hadn't felt this utterly torn apart since Clannad, and my soul and ego had been dealt a huge blow. When I saw the movie which connects Season 1 and 2, I wanted to physically bring characters of the show to life and thrash them, because any feeling other than what I was feeling at that moment in time, would've been better.  When I attempted to start Season 2, for the first time in my life (in any aspect of life), I had to stop. I saw what the season could do to me, and I was afraid. There are times when you go through life changing events, I've been through quite a few, highs and lows although more highs, but when I saw what season 2 brought to the table, I stopped, took a breath and said "I'm not ready". I actually felt like if I proceeded with the show, something inside me would snap or break, and I was not ready.  I'm sure one day I'll come back to it, Gigguk's high praise makes me want to finish it right now, but despite every trial I've been through in my entire life, somehow, this anime about a hole and children is the hardest I will have undergone to date.  I sincerely hope everyone watches the show or at least attempts to watch it. It's beautiful, and I love it, but for the same reason I love it so much, I will watch it only once and never come back (unlike countless other favorites I've rewatched dozens of times)  Source: an ordinary anime fan

I'm Glad Bocchi got as high  as it did, though I think Garnt didn't touch on something that helps to elevate Bocchi: The attention to detail both with animation and story. You don't just see anime characters handling instruments and music plays, you see the characters *playing* the instruments. Every chord, every drumbeat, every bassline; all of it is animated with an attention to detail that boggles the mind. And the story is one that is so true to the life of a small, starting musician, that it has been praised for exactly that by so many people.   I liked a great many anime this year, and many of the ones Gigguk mentioned are also among my favourites, but Bocchi, for me, is by far the best one I watched. For all the reasons he mentioned, and for the ones he did not.

Bocchi was mid. Had 'cute girls doing cute things' but Tatami Galaxy did the 'Just like me FR' better with better writing and more interesting art. However, it didn't have 'cute girlz doing cute things' and the dialogue is too fast for the average anime viewer to keep up with.  Summertime Render is literally the worst writing in anime I've seen in years. I genuinely cannot fathom why anyone with long term reading/anime watching experience would call it anything better than mid. It has good art and decent animation but the writing is atrocious. One moment the MC is this genius detective and in the next he's going around asking random people if they have seen X even when he already saw they were dangerous and willing to kill. Then you have all the tropes of old 90's horror. Like my favorite 'Lets split up' even though the MC knows at that point that they take on the appearance of others. Writer can't decide 'is he smart or a damn vegetable?'  Call of the Night: It's basically Twilight but with good music.  Gundam the Witch of Wokeness. Minority discrimination, Xenophobia, Capitalism bad, Strong independent wahmen etc. Trash.  Cyberpunk Edgerunner had good music, great art and very good animation but shit pacing. The real reason you felt whiplash after each episode is because of how quickly the story goes from a delinquent kid in school to a dropout doing illegal activities to feels trips is fucking fast. The worst pacing is at the start though with how quickly the mother died. It had 0 impact on me because we hardly knew her but the show plays it out as if we should have cared. It managed to give me 'feelz' but that doesn't make it 10/10. It's pacing issues persist and I'd argue it's an 8/10 because of it. Still great but not worth the extreme praise people give it because they felt 'feelz'.

2022 has been a spectacular year for anime, with titles like Demon Slayer, Attack on Titan, and Chainsaw Man setting the bar for stellar animation and storytelling. Edit after seeing the video: Seems like even though I haven't seen much I have finished the entire Top 10 (-Bocchi which is on my watch list) I didn't vibe with Witch of Mercury, Spy X Family or Cyberpunk that much. Mob Psycho was good but I didn't vibe with it that much either (which was also true for previous seasons). Demon Slayer is also in that category of great animation but subpar storytelling for me. I feel like Kaguya and Made in Abyss are multiple steps above these in terms of writing. I love the cast of Kaguya so much because the show seems to love them. Just a stellar production all around.
